<script>
  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_715214ba-fe45-4c87-a21f-022f1028a419'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

      $('edition_35840488').observe('prototip:shown', function() {
        if (this.up('#box')) {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: $('box').getStyle('z-index')})});

      newTip['wrapper'].addClassName('prototipAllowOverflow');

        $('edition_35840488').observe('prototip:shown', function () {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function (e) {
            if ($('edition_35840488').hasClassName('ignored')) {
              e.setStyle({'display': 'none'});
              return;

            e.setStyle({'overflow': 'visible'});
          });

<span class='communityAnswererName'>

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<div class='spoiler'>
This answer contains spoilers…
<span class='spoilerAnswerText'>
<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  
    I think he is still alive... I was a little confused, but I'm guessing he's not actually dead, he was able to get away. Also, I think this is a lot li<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">…more</a>
    I think he is still alive... I was a little confused, but I'm guessing he's not actually dead, he was able to get away. Also, I think this is a lot like X-Men. (Do not keep reading if you don't want X-Men spoilers!!) I think that Max's absorption only affects the prodigy for a little bit, but they eventually recover. (Like Magneto and the X-Men "cure"). So I think Ace was able to recover, but Max still kept his powers. So maybe he has just been hiding away, waiting for his powers to be back at full strength... Thanks! Hope that made sense<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">(less)</a>
  
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>
</span>

<div id="review_1622736444" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1622736444" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1622736444?book_show_action=true">Apr 27, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2017">2017</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1622736444" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5013383834686664013">2 1/2 stars. <br/><br/>I'm reminding myself while I'm writing this that I really didn't like Meyer's <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/36381037.Cinder__The_Lunar_Chronicles___1_' title='Cinder (The Lunar Chronicles, #1) by Marissa Meyer' rel='nofollow noopener'>Cinder</a> but went on to enjoy the rest of the series. Maybe Meyer is just not great at beginnings. Maybe I'm already feeling burned out on this new "It" genre featuring superhero stories. All I know is that <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/28421168.Renegades__Renegades___1_' title='Renegades (Renegades, #1) by Marissa Meyer' rel='nofollow noopener'>Renegades</a> didn't really pick up until the second half and, looking back, I don't get the sense that this first book really had a story arc. There was no climax or revelation. <b>It felt like one very long in</b></span>
  <span id="freeText5013383834686664013" style="display:none">2 1/2 stars. <br /><br />I'm reminding myself while I'm writing this that I really didn't like Meyer's <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/36381037.Cinder__The_Lunar_Chronicles___1_" title="Cinder (The Lunar Chronicles, #1) by Marissa Meyer" rel="nofollow noopener">Cinder</a> but went on to enjoy the rest of the series. Maybe Meyer is just not great at beginnings. Maybe I'm already feeling burned out on this new "It" genre featuring superhero stories. All I know is that <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/28421168.Renegades__Renegades___1_" title="Renegades (Renegades, #1) by Marissa Meyer" rel="nofollow noopener">Renegades</a> didn't really pick up until the second half and, looking back, I don't get the sense that this first book really had a story arc. There was no climax or revelation. <b>It felt like one very long introduction.</b><br /><br />For much of the book, this feels like a very standard superhero tale that doesn't do anything new. After an age of anarchy descended and gangs ruled the streets, the Renegades emerged to restore the balance with their superpowers. Now they rule the city. The orphaned Nova, however, feels they are the reason her parents were murdered and so she teams up with the other side - the Anarchists - in order to overthrow the Renegades.<br /><br />It was almost unreadable at first, with the <b>cliche dialogue</b> making it seem as if the characters were reading off the script for the latest superhero movie:<br /><blockquote>
  <i>"Nightmare," said Smokescreen, with a subtle incline of his head. "It's been a while."<br />"You're about to wish it had been longer."<br />***<br />"Your days of villainy are over, Nightmare."</i>
</blockquote><br />Both characters and scenes seem stolen straight from Marvel. Frostbite is obviously a play on Storm from X-men, right down to the “silver-white hair”. Gargoyle is a Hulk-like monster. They are not developed far beyond the description of their powers, which makes it difficult to distinguish them from the superheroes we know. Similarly, the parade attack near the beginning will surely remind many readers of the Green Goblin vs Spiderman parade attack. <br /><br />And how is it possible that no-one worked out that Adrian is the Sentinel? Honestly, how? The Sentinel is a mysterious new superhero who claims he is a Renegade and Adrian suddenly disappears every time he’s around. Plus everyone knows how much both Adrian and the Sentinel want to find Nightmare… how do they not know? He is the worst at having a secret identity. (Note: this is not a spoiler. We are told his identity in the beginning.)<br /><br /><b>It's a long book for YA and it feels even longer</b>. Though it does pick up eventually, I thought it was too little, too late. I will probably read on with the series, if only because I learned once already that Meyer builds up to the goods. But my expectations have been dramatically lowered. <br /><br />Diversity points for the Italian-Filipina protagonist, Adrian's two dads, and a character with a disability. <br /><br /><a href="http://thebookgeek.org" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thebookgeekreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookgeek01" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://instagram.com/emleemay" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/EmilyMayTheBookGeek" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="5013383834686664013" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2216338904" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2216338904" />
    <a title="Emma Giordano" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30604861-emma-giordano"><img alt="Emma Giordano" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1569693958p2/30604861.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2216338904?book_show_action=true">Jan 19, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emma Giordano" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emma Giordano" href="/user/show/30604861-emma-giordano">Emma Giordano</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30604861-emma-giordano?shelf=audiobooks">audiobooks</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2216338904" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16227635035608344887">I LOVED THIS BOOK SO MUCH. So fun so complex so interesting – a must read!! Check out my video review!: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=veujVwZolNw'>https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=veujV...</a><br/><br/>Other than the epic superheroes, what intrigues me most about <i>Renegades</i> is that it focuses on the concept of anarchy, which appears to be lacking in YA despite the abundance of dystopian/futuristic novels already on the market. The history of the time of anarchy combined with active anarchists in the present story made it very unique in that manner. I cl</span>
  <span id="freeText16227635035608344887" style="display:none">I LOVED THIS BOOK SO MUCH. So fun so complex so interesting – a must read!! Check out my video review!: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=veujVwZolNw">https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=veujV...</a><br /><br />Other than the epic superheroes, what intrigues me most about <i>Renegades</i> is that it focuses on the concept of anarchy, which appears to be lacking in YA despite the abundance of dystopian/futuristic novels already on the market. The history of the time of anarchy combined with active anarchists in the present story made it very unique in that manner. I clearly don’t agree with total anarchy, but the state of the world before and after that period is truly fascinating and leads to a variety of moral questions to toy with while reading. <br /><br />Although there is an influx of superhero content in the entertainment world as of late, I still feel as if <i> Renegades</i> stands on its own. I’m not a Marvel/DC fan in the slightest and superhero films/comic books are not my thing, but the dynamics of the prodigies vs. the Renegades vs. the Anarchists vs. the public were too fascinating for me to scoff at. The powers of prodigies vary from invulnerability and elemental manipulation to the ability to make origami come to life – the variety in terms of powers and standards created by both the superheroes and the public was very interesting to me. I found all the abilities to be well-though-out consistent, and the increase in scope of powers to be extremely well done. I definitely feel this novel would appeal to non-superhero fans who are still intrigued by the concept of supernatural abilities.<br /><br />I LOVED the characters in this story. For a SFF YA novel, we have a very diverse cast which I was super pleased with! One of our main characters is Italian/Filipina, and the other is described as having “brown skin”; Additionally, one of them comes from a household with two dads and another superhero side character is disabled (walks with a cane &amp; his superpower has nothing to do with his disability!) Nova is fierce, resourceful, brave, and confident – I truly enjoyed reading from her perspective. Adrian is also brave and intent on justice, but I feel we see more of his soft side as the story progresses. I found most of characters to be interesting and complex.<br /><br />I REALLY enjoyed the slight romance in this story, more than I have regarding YA books in a while. It is the definition of slow burn, and even by the ending, romantic feelings are only just developing. The story is definitely centered on the dynamics between Renegades and Anarchists, with romance being one of the least important parts of the plot in my opinion. It’s the type of relationship where the flirtations and growth of feelings are only just beginning to brew, but you still REALLY want to root for the characters to be together.<br /><br />Overall, <i>Renegades</i> was a fantastic read (and a fantastic audiobook!) I would absolutely recommend this read, particularly to those interested in SFF, supernatural powers, complex moral issues, and unbelievable twists. This one is definitely on my list of auto-recommends!</span>
  <a data-text-id="16227635035608344887" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

<span id="freeTextContainer8035386847113726637">I’ve got like, two feelings about this book and not all of them are good.<br/><br/>I'm trying to come to terms with the possibility that I will never form a meaningful emotional connection with a Marissa Meyer book like I did with The Lunar Chronicles. It's like my heart closes for maintenance when it comes to anything else written by this author. I don't know. There must have been a dimensional hiccup in the timeline—how else could I go from being unambiguously and obsessively 100% full scale high key ad</span>
  <span id="freeText8035386847113726637" style="display:none">I’ve got like, two feelings about this book and not all of them are good.<br /><br />I'm trying to come to terms with the possibility that I will never form a meaningful emotional connection with a Marissa Meyer book like I did with The Lunar Chronicles. It's like my heart closes for maintenance when it comes to anything else written by this author. I don't know. There must have been a dimensional hiccup in the timeline—how else could I go from being unambiguously and obsessively 100% full scale high key addicted to her books to just....being an aggressively disinterested bystander?<br /><br />Aaaaad here's why:<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b> ✨<u> THE ‘MEH’ FACTOR:</u></b>
</blockquote><br /><br />Renegades was one big conglomerate of timeworn clichés and hackneyed superhero tropes, which would have gotten me so pumped—like, who cares? it’s time to read about overthrowing the government and burning the patriarchy to the ground—if at least the MCs managed to scratch a line into my heart. But they didn't. I don't dislike them really, I'm just like “meh ok, go do your thing in your corner”. The secondary characers also had so much potential yet they eventually became a distant memory. They kind of just existed in the nook of the MCs', like some ghosts of goodwill. No witty banter to make them stand out or anything. There were like two characters who would’ve made this book a lot better but none of them were given enough backstory or enough page time..<br /><br />Honestly, I think the main problem is that when I think about this book…I don’t feel anything. My mind just blanks and all I feel is hollow wind blowing through my skull because it's just kind of there... trying so hard but failing to leave even the most basic impression upon my psyche. Yes, it was fun to read for a couple of pages but the love just isn’t there. Swipe left. <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>✨ <u>IT WAS TEXTBOOK KIND OF LONG</u></b>
</blockquote><br /><br />One of the biggest disconnects from this book is how much pages it took. You could shrink up at least 40% of it into a little nice blot. Instead, it was too long and too introductory and I kept losing track of the story after 10 consecutive pages of redundant descriptions. I was just SO BORED. I couldn't read a couple of pages without also being on my phone watching vine compilations.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>✨<u> C FOR CLICHE</u>:</b>
</blockquote><br /><br />I really wish there was a camera following me around 24/7 so whenever something completely predictable and unoriginal happened, so I could look directly into the camera like in The Office. <br /><br />• This is your painfully <i>typical</i> <b>Supervillains vs Superheroes story</b>. The Anarchists are the supervillains in this case, and of course like any other superhero comic/book/movie, they're actually the ones with a vision for the world. The Anarchists are trying to change things for all prodigies and fight their oppressors. The Renegades are resisting that change and their only goal seems to be stoping the villains from reaching <i>their</i> goal. <br /><br />• <b>Overused and generic tragic backstories</b>. I mean, of course it’s not a superhero novel without a few sob stories. What these kids need is extensive sessions of therapy where they can unload their heavy emotional baggage. Just saying.<br /><br />• <b>Cheesy villainous dialogue</b> that only gives the superheroes a chance to turn the tables.... except of course they never do. The monologues were so cringy I almost eye-rolled into another dimension. Yikes.<br /><br />• <b>Secret identities</b>. Duh. At least, it would’ve been much better if their secret identities was actually <i>secret</i>, so the readers have to try and figure it out. But what's absolutely unrefined WILD to me, however, is that no one, NOT ONE SINGLE CHARACTER, was able to come across two brain cells to rub together and figure out that Adrian was the Sentinel and that Nova was Nightmare. The fact that Adrian and Nova suddenly disappear EVERY TIME their alter egos show up is the equivalent of venomous animals being bright orange. Imagine “HEY WE HAVE SECRET IDENTITIES” written in sixty stores high letters and there's a bone fire in the middle....that's how <i>obvious</i> it was.<br /><br />• <b>The plot twists were so...anticlimactic.</b> I would have loved to be passionate and react but when it all played out, I went like, [monotone voice] wow ok. Like, you know in the metamorphosis, when Gregor wakes up and instead of freaking out because holy! shit! he’s a bug, he’s just like “I really cannot deal with this right now”. That was me after every single reveal.<br /><br />At this point, I'm frankly more interested in reading about the insurance adjuster who arrives to assess damage after superhero fights and starts an investigation to uncover their real identities and hold them accountable for all the property damage they've caused.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>✨ <u>THE ROMANCE</u></b>
</blockquote><br /><br />This is a public service announcement: I do not care one single bit about the romance in this book. Get it away from me. Do not touch me with their romantic sentiment. <br /><br />I'm not even going to give a valid reason, it's just the good ol' unwarranted dislike. They annoy me and that's the end of it. I also have so much beef with the concept of “<i>having</i> to ship off all your main characters into clichéd hetero relationships”. Their banter was the equivalent of slightly stale piece of bread. THEY DONT EVEN <i>LIKE</i> EACH OTHER OR EVEN HAVE FUN TOGETHER. Thank you, next.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>✨ <u>POSITIVE NOTES</u></b>
</blockquote><br /><br />Okay here's what I liked, because I'm not completely a swamp goblin lol.<br /><br />• <b>DIVERSITY.</b><br /><br />Nova is half Filipino. Adrian has two supportive and happily married dads. Oscar has a rare bone disease that rendered him disabled.<br /><br />•<b> MAX.</b><br /><br />Max is a 10 years old kid with a mysterious and highly dangerous superpower. He's been put in quarantine because of the aformentioned superpower but can we please take a minute of our time to appreciate what a pure source of light and warmth he is? I wish I had big tender wings to protect him. He’s literally the only reason I didn't call this book a dnf and spare myself the stress pimples.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8035386847113726637" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2059192162" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2059192162" />
    <a title="emma" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/32879029-emma"><img alt="emma" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1520568130p2/32879029.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2059192162?book_show_action=true">Jul 13, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="emma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="emma" href="/user/show/32879029-emma">emma</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=diverse">diverse</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=eh">eh</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=comments">comments</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=owned">owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=auto-buy-authors">auto-buy-authors</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=3-stars">3-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=couldn-t-wait-to-read">couldn-t-wait-to-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2059192162" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6108544165644001244">Guys, I don’t know myself anymore.<br/><br/>I’m currently sitting here eating baby carrots, and I’m not happy about it, which is characteristic, but the sheer fact that I’m ingesting a vegetable in the first place is astounding. I’m currently addicted to watching feature-length episodes of a British quiz show on YouTube, when up until two days ago I was convinced I was racist against British people. But most importantly (and actually, you know, semi-relevantly) I don’t know how I feel about Marissa Meyer.</span>
  <span id="freeText6108544165644001244" style="display:none">Guys, I don’t know myself anymore.<br><br>I’m currently sitting here eating baby carrots, and I’m not happy about it, which is characteristic, but the sheer fact that I’m ingesting a vegetable in the first place is astounding. I’m currently addicted to watching feature-length episodes of a British quiz show on YouTube, when up until two days ago I was convinced I was racist against British people. But most importantly (and actually, you know, semi-relevantly) I don’t know how I feel about Marissa Meyer.<br><br><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://emmareadstoomuch.wordpress.com/2018/11/06/disappointment-and-an-existential-crisis-renegades-and-archenemies-reviews/">https://emmareadstoomuch.wordpress.co...</a><br><br>She used to be my Favorite Author!!! (Capitals and excessive exclamation points for both emphasis and flair.) Or I used to say she was. Because I also used to say that the Lunar Chronicles were my favorite series, before I realized that was patently false.<br><br>But now there’s a whole lot going on.<br><br>I do remember loving all of the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/list/32879029-emma?utf8=%E2%9C%93&amp;search%5Bquery%5D=marissa+meyer" rel="nofollow noopener">Lunar Chronicles</a> books except <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1237784650" rel="nofollow noopener">Cinder</a>, which was meh. Well, and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1354779723" rel="nofollow noopener">Fairest</a> was pretty bad. Okay and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1876335336" rel="nofollow noopener">Wires and Nerve</a> was also bad. But anyway, I read most of them in 2015 and 2015 me, as has been stated many a time on this account, canNOT be trusted. Example of an opinion I held in 2015, for proof: “I should wear full makeup, including eyeliner, to school every day. Even though school starts at 7:35 a.m. Even though I could sleep for at least 14 more minutes if I, you know, didn’t do that.”<br><br>See the level of illogical we’re working with when we reflect on 2015?<br><br>Anyway. But it gets worse, because I hated the book <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1627441958" rel="nofollow noopener">Heartless</a> with everything in me. Which caught me off guard, because that was in very early 2017 and I hadn’t realized past me’s lack of reliability yet.<br><br>The point of all of this is that I approached this book with trepidation. And now I am approaching this review with trepidation, because I DON’T KNOW HOW I FEEL!!<br><br>Yes, I am claiming to be “approaching” this review even as I am clearly an excessive number of words into it. What of it?<br><br>Let’s divide this into two very broad categories. Bad news first.<br><br><br><b>THE BAD</b><br><br>I am currently taking a class called “The Art of Fiction,” and it has threatened to single-handedly absolutely full-on ruin reading one hundred percent of YA fantasy for me. Just in time for me to be in the hugest fantasy mood of my life!! Ideal. Life is filled with these perfect symmetries, etc.<br><br>Anyway. In that course, we read a couple of stories by Anton Chekhov, and Chekhov’s got this quote, maybe, which may or may not go something like this: “If you say in the first chapter that there is a rifle hanging on the wall, in the second or third chapter it absolutely must go off. If it's not going to be fired, it shouldn't be hanging there.” This is a very great quote to ponder as a writer, but as a reader it sucks SO BAD.<br><br>No twist is a twist anymore. I see everything coming. I am now prescient and it is a goddamn curse.<br><br>Basically what I’m saying is that I saw a twist in this book coming and I blame Chekhov.<br><br>My more major, less literary complaint: the pacing of this is extremely strange. I think that has a lot to do with the fact that this book is FIVE HUNDRED PAGES LONG!! Can you imagine being bold enough to make the <i>first book</i> in your trilogy five hundred pages long?? Who besides Marissa Meyer has the clout to pull that type of sh*t off.<br><br>But anyway. As the old saying goes, just because Marissa Meyer can doesn’t mean Marissa Meyer should. There is just no reason this book had to be 500 pages long. One, because that’s too long for almost any book, but two, because this book was doing absolutely nothing good with all of those pages.<br><br>First off, I finished this book and was like, “Ah! A whole lot of nothing.” It truly feels like there is absolutely zero plotline to this book. There are a few separate events with very little tying them together, and definitely no tension or suspense of any kind. The last hundred pages especially were like Dry City, USA. (Dry meaning boring. Not as in “not wet.” Hopefully all pages are Dry City, USA in that sense.)<br><br>The second pacing thing: this felt like 1.5 books. I can pick an exact moment around 350 pages in that felt like a perfect stopping point, but this bad boy just...trucks on. And not only does that 350 page mark feel like a perfect ending, the actual ending (150 pages or so later) feels like the exact middle point of a book.<br><br>The ending was so, so, so weird and so, so, so rushed. I’m going to say what happened that was very strange in vague terms, so hopefully I won’t spoil anything, but if you haven’t read the book just skip this paragraph maybe. Okay so basically, one character has a near-death experience and we are expected to believe this character died. However, this character did NOT die. Character tricked us and other characters! That is just so classic this character. Anyway, character pops up, alive and well, and <i>no explanation is ever given for how this character didn’t die.</i> We just move on!<br><br>Sloppy, sloppy. I’m honestly very glad I have the ARC of Archenemies. not because this is so good that I’m like, let me get my hands on that sequel, but more because this feels aggressively unfinished.<br><br>In terms of characters: I feel pretty meh about all of them. There were some that have potential (more on that later), but a few were so devastatingly devoid of personality that a side-by-side comparison between them and a sleeve of saltines would make the crackers seem like a day trip to Flavortown. (Guy Fieri reference: Check.)<br><br>Finally, this book often just felt like...nothing special. Superheroes have been done. Slow burn romances and banter and fight scenes every hundred pages and halfhearted twists have been done. At a lot of moments this just felt like every entry into the superhero genre tossed in a blender with every YA fantasy of the last five years.<br><br>And that’s really lame.<br><br>Luckily, we left the good stuff to cheer ourselves up!!<br><br><br><b>THE GOOD</b><br><br>Even though this was unoriginal, it still managed to be...kind of fun? And a way quicker read than any poorly-structured book over five hundred pages has any right to be. At the beginning of the month, I was STRESSING about the idea of reading 1000 pages of Marissa Meyer superhero content on top of, like, midterms and basic human responsibilities.<br><br>But it seems to be going peachily. (Massive shoutout to Google Drive for not marking the adverb version of “peachy” I just made up a spelling error. I feel like a linguistic prophet.)<br><br>Also, I think Marissa Meyer puts forth a good effort in terms of diversity in this book. And she kind of always has. Cinder came out in 2013, back when SJM was just writing undiverse books instead of undiverse books feigning diversity, and presumably when JK Rowling’s Twitter was something other than a nonstop fountain flowing with cringe. Cinder is pretty diverse, considering.<br><br>Marissa Meyer has always seemed to me like one of the only YA authors who may actually care about diversity for diversity’s sake, rather than point-scoring. Which is rad.<br><br>There’s also a really interesting exploration of good versus evil and moral ambiguity in this book. Essentially what Wildcard stumbled over itself trying to do, except this was actually remotely good. And also this wasn’t constantly interrupting itself to have its female protagonist moon over a very annoying and morally corrupt man.<br><br>Other good things: I don’t know if this is fully one hundred percent unambiguously good, but I think there is POTENTIAL for me liking these characters. I am the closest to liking Nova. If a seven on the ten-point love scale is “truly like,” I am probably at 5.5 with her. Close second, Oscar, then Ruby, then Honey, then Adrian. If Archenemies really puts in work, I may end up liking one or two of them.<br><br>There is absolutely no question of me possibly liking any other character in this series.<br><br>But here is the single most surprising thing I liked about this series, and I’m almost embarrassed to say it…<br><br>Okay, FINE. It was the romance! I liked the romance.<br><br>It’s nice. It’s slow burn. The characters are awkward and both like nO STOP I DON’T LIKE ANYONE. I AM THE VOID. I FEEL NOTHING. Which is very fun. I think they’re a good match and oh my god I am going to go lay in a pond now since when do I say things like “a good match.”<br><br>Closing out this review like we started it: With me having a minor existential crisis over my own identity.<br><br>Bottom line: This was not <i>good</i>, per se, but it was fun and fine!<br><br><br>----------<br><br>"I can't wait to read this book," I say, and then wait almost a year before reading this book<br><br><s>please be better than Heartless</s><br><br>----------<br><br>I can't forget the pain Heartless caused me, but Marissa...I'm willing to forgive.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1499984798ra/23287302.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="6108544165644001244" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2135071148" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2135071148" />
    <a title="Melanie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3030788-melanie"><img alt="Melanie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577914102p2/3030788.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2135071148?book_show_action=true">Sep 25, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melanie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melanie" href="/user/show/3030788-melanie">Melanie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=read-in-2018">read-in-2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=audible">audible</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=buddy-reads">buddy-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2135071148" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13078783004887517707"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1516566877i/24897415._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Hero or villain, all prodigies were powerful. All prodigies were dangerous.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/>Me and Marissa Meyer have an all over the place relationship. I wasn’t the biggest fan of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1494277256?book_show_action=false' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Lunar Chronicles</a>, but I love Scarlet and Wolf! But my favorite thing she’s ever created was <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1499783627' rel='nofollow noopener'>Heartless</a>, which I five starred and it made it onto my best of list the year it came out. So, I didn’t know what to expect going into <i>Renegades</i>. I wasn’t even going to pick it up originally, but I did solely because I saw a G</span>
  <span id="freeText13078783004887517707" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1516566877i/24897415._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Hero or villain, all prodigies were powerful. All prodigies were dangerous.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>Me and Marissa Meyer have an all over the place relationship. I wasn’t the biggest fan of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1494277256?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">The Lunar Chronicles</a>, but I love Scarlet and Wolf! But my favorite thing she’s ever created was <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1499783627" rel="nofollow noopener">Heartless</a>, which I five starred and it made it onto my best of list the year it came out. So, I didn’t know what to expect going into <i>Renegades</i>. I wasn’t even going to pick it up originally, but I did solely because I saw a Goodreads review being disgusting about there being two gay dads that raised one of the main protagonists. TL;DR - I loved the gay dads, but I only ended up liking <i>Renegades</i>. <br><br><i>Renegades</i> is set in a world where people rely on superheroes. The superheroes come with a vast array of powers and abilities, but with superheroes, there are always supervillains, too! Yet, the supervillains are more of rebels with superpowers, and they call themselves the Anarchists! <br><br>Our main protagonist, Nova, was raised to believe in the Renegades and to trust in the hope that they provide. But that all changed the night she was orphaned, and no one came to save her or her family. Since then she has had only one mission: to get vengeance for her family. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“One cannot be brave who has no fear.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>Also, I couldn’t write this review without mentioning that Nova (AKA: Nightmare and Insomnia) is Italian-Filipina, and this made my little Filipina heart so very full of happiness. Also, Nova’s super power is sleep manipulation, which was totally unique and super badass, in my opinion. Also, I’m forever living for morally grey characters that are constantly questioning the motives all around them, so Nova was a damn treat to read about. <br><br>The other main protagonist is Adrian (AKA: the Sentinal and Sketch), who happens to have the two kickass, gay, famous, superhero dads! His power is pretty OP; as long as he believes something is plausible, he can draw it and give it the desired effect. Like, it’s kind of complicated, but he can pretty much draw things and make them a reality. <br><br>And obviously Nova and Adrian’s lives intertwine and a lot of events ensue. And, if you’ve ever read a book by Marissa Meyer before, you can probably guess that a romance happens as well. Now, forbidden romance is kind of my favorite, and I was here for it, but I will say that it was a little cliché at times. <br><br>But this is a story about secrets, filled with characters that are playing both sides for the Renegades and for the Anarchists. This story is filled with twists and turns, and you’ll never really know who to root for, which is pretty amazing. <br><br>Yet, this is also a story about questioning what is good and bad. And how things that present themselves as good aren’t always the way they seem. I think it’s important for kids and teens to be reading about questioning the world around them right now, and I really liked the discussion that could be had here from these themes that were presented. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“If people wanted to stand up for themselves or protect their loved ones or do what they believe in their hearts is the right thing to do, then they would do it. If they wanted to be heroic, they would find ways to be heroic, even without supernatural powers.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>Now, let me also say that I read this via audiobook, and I am the worst audiobook reader ever. I just have a really hard time focusing, and I’ll try to listen while I play <i>League of Legends</i>, and then I’ll end up not retaining anything, and I’ll have to go relisten. This book took me a month to read, which is unheard of for me. I strongly believe that if I read this book physically that I would have enjoyed it even more. And I completely plan to do so with the next book! <br><br>Overall, if you like superhero books then you will probably really enjoy this one. Sometimes I did feel like maybe a few elements were pulled too strongly from <i>X-Men</i> (*cough ROGUE cough*), but Marissa Meyer’s writing is always easy to read and fun to follow. The story had a bit of racial diversity, sexual diversity, and a disabled side-character that I really appreciated. Also, please give me an entire book of just Max, thanks. But I think most people that have enjoyed previous things by this author will also really enjoy this one! I’m excited to see what happens next, especially with that ending. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“There are many dangerous people in this world. But there are also many good people. Brave people. No matter how bad things get, we have to remember that.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><a href="https://meltotheany.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.twitter.com/meltotheany" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://meltotheany.tumblr.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Tumblr</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/meltotheany/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/channel/UC4RbHEg_fH6CewJrh_0xJ9g" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a href="http://www.twitch.tv/meltotheany" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitch</a><br><br>Buddy Read with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/40275186-sarah" rel="nofollow noopener">Sarah</a> &amp; <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/17290119-rachel-typed-truths" rel="nofollow noopener">Rachel</a>! ❤</span>
  <a data-text-id="13078783004887517707" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2180177461" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Cristina Monica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica"><img alt="Cristina Monica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589617514p2/14596170.jpg" /></a>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

        <a title="Cristina Monica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cristina Monica" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica">Cristina Monica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=superheroes">superheroes</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=vendetta">vendetta</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=action">action</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2180177461" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2771836069239918759">From fairytale retellings to... Marvel-reminiscent superheroes. <br/><br/>Did anyone expect it? I didn't. In my mind, Marissa Meyer still had Beauty and the Beast, The Little Mermaid, hell The Princess and the Frog, as well as many other fairytales to write entire books about. <br/><br/>But you have to admire her(?) decision to write about something different. She has no idea if her new series will be well-received or completely hated, and yet she still dared to write what she felt was right to her, not what everyo</span>
  <span id="freeText2771836069239918759" style="display:none">From fairytale retellings to... Marvel-reminiscent superheroes. <br /><br />Did anyone expect it? I didn't. In my mind, Marissa Meyer still had Beauty and the Beast, The Little Mermaid, hell The Princess and the Frog, as well as many other fairytales to write entire books about. <br /><br />But you have to admire her(?) decision to write about something different. She has no idea if her new series will be well-received or completely hated, and yet she still dared to write what she felt was right to her, not what everyone (like me) expected her to. <br /><br />The writing is strong, but then again what is new? Marissa Meyer can start writing adult horror books with freaky dead dolls creeping into your brain and the writing would be incredible nonetheless. (I hope she doesn't, though.) <br /><br />I even enjoyed the story. If I'm not forgetting any past reads, this is my first superhero book read – or one of the firsts – so I was certainly very interested from the beginning, and my interest remained long enough for me to finish these 478 pages in a considerably short time. <br /><br />Sadly, I have to complain about the overused storyline idea of the child seeking revenge for the death of his/her parents. What I love about vendetta stories is how fierce and determined the revengeful ones are and how important justice – though not exactly the right kind – is to them, which we have here. However, I have to admit that vendetta stories can get repetitive, so not everything in here is original. <br /><br />Plus good vs. evil fighting against each other because they each believe their own worldviews trump the other's? Meh. <br /><br />But as I mentioned, I was still very interested, because Marissa Meyer knows how to make the reader want more, with small twists and turns hidden at various places inside the storyline, and by making us curious about the future of the characters, whether we're fully invested in them or just a little. And it's true the characters grow on you, even if in the beginning you're not so sure. <br /><br />I would suggest Ms. Meyer practiced writing fighting action scenes more, though, since they do feel rehearsed. I had trouble taking some of them seriously. <br /><br />Would recommend. <br /><br /><a href="https://hitormissbooks.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/LolaReviewer" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a>Twitter</a> | <a>Instagram</a> | <a href="https://plus.google.com/u/0/105021852309973899120/posts" rel="nofollow noopener">Google+</a> | <a href="https://www.bloglovin.com/blogs/hit-miss-books-12564715" rel="nofollow noopener">Bloglovin’</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="2771836069239918759" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2426504961" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2426504961" />
    <a title="Jessi ♥️ H. Vojsk" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/66224803-jessi-h-vojsk"><img alt="Jessi ♥️ H. Vojsk" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1597641717p2/66224803.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2426504961?book_show_action=true">Sep 18, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessi ♥️ H. Vojsk" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessi ♥️ H. Vojsk" href="/user/show/66224803-jessi-h-vojsk">Jessi ♥️ H. Vojsk</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2426504961" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7182416534738406588"><i> “One cannot be brave who has no fear.” </i> <br/><br/>Story ⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️<br/>In a World Full of People with superpowers, which Side would you choose - good or evil? <br/>Would you be a superhero or a villain? <br/>If I had to choose, I would take the side which would be the right one in my opinion. <br/>That’s what I love about really brilliantly created villains - in their own eyes they do the right thing, they are the heroes.<br/>Nova was raised by people that many call villains - people that fought the Renegades in the Age of Anarc</span>
  <span id="freeText7182416534738406588" style="display:none"><i> “One cannot be brave who has no fear.” </i> <br /><br />Story ⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️<br />In a World Full of People with superpowers, which Side would you choose - good or evil? <br />Would you be a superhero or a villain? <br />If I had to choose, I would take the side which would be the right one in my opinion. <br />That’s what I love about really brilliantly created villains - in their own eyes they do the right thing, they are the heroes.<br />Nova was raised by people that many call villains - people that fought the Renegades in the Age of Anarchy. <br />Now she’s back for revenge - to avenge her uncles death and to destroy the dictatorship of the Renegades.<br />But after a failed assassination on the head of the Renegades, Nova is forced to take another way to get what she wants. <br />And that makes her rethink everything she thought and all her plans. But in the end she’s sure of the things that are right. <br />From the first moment I was absolutely fascinated and in love with this book. <br />Finally a book about superheroes and villains were we get to choose which side we’re on. <br />And I’m definitely Team Nova. <br />And Team Adrian. <br />Oh, oops. <br />That’s not working right? <br />I loved the fight, the twists, the humor and that ending - OH MY GOD. <br />Okay, let’s just say I Love the story and all the characters in it and it’s now one of my favorite series and I can’t wait to read the next book. <br /><br />Character ⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️<br /><i> “Your days of villainy are over, Nightmare."<br />She scoffed. "You sound like you've read too many comics."<br />"You sound like you think that's a bad thing," he retorted. </i> <br />I always had a weakness for villains, for bad boys, for people who were seen as evil. <br />And Nova aka Nightmare is one of them. She attempted to kill one of the Council members of the Renegades- and she failed. <br />But that didn’t stop her. <br />She was ruthless, extremely intelligent and such an interesting character. She did what needed to be done, she sacrificed things for her goals and she never thought to stop thinking about everyone’s life’s. <br />Adrian - my wonderful cinnamon roll - oh, I mean, superhero. He was such a sweetie. <br />He was smart, strong and he knew when Nova could save her own ass. <br />He was also such a lovely and caring son, big brother and team leader.<br />All in all I was absolutely in love with him. <br />Even though I loved all the characters in this book, I still think they need a little bit more depth. But maybe that’ll come with the next book. <br /><br />World ⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️<br /><i> For hundred of years, prodigies were feared by the rest of the world. <br />Ace Anarchy changed everything. He united the most powerful prodigies he could find and together they rebelled. <br />Whole governments, gone. <br />Law enforcement, disbanded. <br />The Anarchists cared little for what would come next once the old world crumbled. <br />They cared only for change, and they got it. <br />Soon, a number of villain gangs began to crawl out from Society’s ashes, each hungry for their own slice of power, and it wasn’t long before Ace Anarchys influence spread across the globe. <br />They call it the Age of Anarchy. <br />But then, seemingly overnight... hope. <br />Bright and sparkling hope, dressed up in capes and masks. <br />Hope called themselves the Renegades. </i> <br />I thought this Pre-Prologue was absolutely perfect. Every time we get to know a little bit more about what happened and what is happening now, I get to excited. <br /><br />Relationships ⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️<br />Of course I’m a sucker for a forbidden love story. The hero and the villain? Hell, Yeah. <br />And the tension and the cuteness between those two was just so beautiful. <br />Next to the sweet relationship Nova and Adrian had, there was also the relationships Nova had with her “family”, the villains. <br />The loyalty she felt towards her uncle, who saved her and the love she felt towards the other villains was so refreshing. <br />She didn’t care who they were to the world, she didn’t care what they did and how they got their villain-names. She only cared how they treated her, how they raised her. <br />And it was so gorgeous and beautiful. <br />I loved it. <br />I loved how Nova saw the world and the people in it. <br /><i> “There are many dangerous people in this world. <br />But there are also many good people. <br />Brave people. <br />No matter how bad things get, we have to remember that. <br />So long as there are heroes in this world, there's hope that tomorrow night might be better.” </i> <br /><br /><br />Writing style ⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️<br />Oh I loved the writing. It was so perfectly paced and balanced, there was action, romantic tension and funny things too. <br />It wasn’t full of beautiful quotes, but there were still some I really loved. <br />All in all I’m absolutely fascinated and happy I started this book. <br />Can’t wait for the next book!<br /><br /><i> “What exactly are we looking for?”<br />“Villains, doing villainous things.” </i></span>
  <a data-text-id="7182416534738406588" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText10617005968195678256" style="display:none">I don’t think I can properly put into words how INCREDIBLE this book was!!!               <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/34410191-emi?shelf=4-stars">4-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/34410191-emi?shelf=2018">2018</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1845080000" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11625789095970191056">I forgot the book ended with that. Holy shit.<br/><br/>This probably would have been a 4 star rating if I found Nova to be a more likable character. But I didn't. So it's not.<br/><br/>Rtc maybe? We'll see. </span>

          </span>

<div id="review_2012928021" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2012928021" />
    <a title="may ➹" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/68157476-may"><img alt="may ➹" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1538949856p2/68157476.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2012928021?book_show_action=true">May 28, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="may ➹" class="user" itemprop="url" name="may ➹" href="/user/show/68157476-may">may ➹</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68157476-may?shelf=dystopian">dystopian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68157476-may?shelf=read-2017">read-2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68157476-may?shelf=pov-multiple">pov-multiple</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68157476-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68157476-may?shelf=2-star">2-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68157476-may?shelf=annoying">annoying</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68157476-may?shelf=disappointing">disappointing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68157476-may?shelf=pov-3rd">pov-3rd</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68157476-may?shelf=diverse">diverse</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68157476-may?shelf=boring">boring</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2012928021" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1353970995279486992"><b>PSA: THIS BOOK SUCKED BUT NOT BECAUSE OF THE GAY DADS</b><br/><br/>I don’t think anything Marissa Meyer writes will ever live up to the series that <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/series/62018-the-lunar-chronicles' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Lunar Chronicles</a> was, because this was HORRIBLE in comparison to that. I could’ve reread the whole Lunar Chronicles series in the time it took me to finish this AND enjoyed it all much more than this one.<br/><br/><blockquote>🌹 <u><b>PLOT</b></u></blockquote><br/>My main problem here is with <b>HOW. SLOW. IT. WAS.</b> For a book this size, it should’ve been action-packed & engaging & fast-paced. It wasn’t. <br/><br/>It took until</span>
  <span id="freeText1353970995279486992" style="display:none"><b>PSA: THIS BOOK SUCKED BUT NOT BECAUSE OF THE GAY DADS</b><br /><br />I don’t think anything Marissa Meyer writes will ever live up to the series that <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/62018-the-lunar-chronicles" rel="nofollow noopener">The Lunar Chronicles</a> was, because this was HORRIBLE in comparison to that. I could’ve reread the whole Lunar Chronicles series in the time it took me to finish this AND enjoyed it all much more than this one.<br /><br /><blockquote>🌹 <u><b>PLOT</b></u></blockquote><br />My main problem here is with <b>HOW. SLOW. IT. WAS.</b> For a book this size, it should’ve been action-packed &amp; engaging &amp; fast-paced. It wasn’t. <br /><br />It took until 50% to actually start getting interesting, and by that time we were 250 pages in. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16143347.We_Were_Liars" title="We Were Liars by E. Lockhart" rel="nofollow noopener">We Were Liars</a> is a thriller that takes place in 250 pages and manages to fit in an introduction, a complex conflict, an intriguing storyline, a plot twist, AND a satisfying conclusion. I had so many emotions during those 250 pages. And Renegades? <b>I felt nothing but remorse for my mother &amp; myself for making her spend money on getting this for me as a birthday gift.</b> I demand a refund on the $20 spent on this &amp; also every high expectation I had on this book.<br /><br />But even after 50%, I barely remember any of the events that happened??? <b>I felt so disconnected &amp; distracted</b> to actually READ &amp; ENJOY the book, despite trying so hard to love it.<br /><br />Like you know when you’re lying down on the beach and trying to enjoy the beautiful sunset but you just can’t stop thinking about how global warming is going to make this part of the ocean flood the entire beach &amp; land and suddenly it’s all ruined for you?? THAT WAS THIS BOOK.<br /><br />Oh, and besides me being able to guess what the plot twist was even tho I suck at predicting, <b>the plot twist wasn’t even well-executed</b>. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Referring to the dead person with the past tense when they know that person ISN’T dead?? Yes, makes for a plot twist, but no, not a good one. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><blockquote>🌷 <u><b>CHARACTERS</b><u></u></u></blockquote><br /><b>There were way too many characters introduced at the beginning</b> (as well as lots of info-dumping of characters’ backstories instead of spreading it out a bit more) that made it super confusing. Like first of all, I have the Renegades to remember. Then the Anarchists, then the Council members. But OH NO, I forgot that EVERY single one of those characters has an alias so I have to remember those too!!!<br /><br />// <b>NOVA</b>: I literally do not care for her at all. She could’ve been such an intriguing character with an intricate backstory. <b>She was a FAKE morally ambiguous villain</b> and I was so mad!!! The only time I actually liked her was at the end, even though she went through no development at all except for “Renegades are EVIL”—“okay I do not like a Renegade that’s forbidden”—“okay so maybe Renegades aren’t that bad”—“Renegades are EVIL”. <br /><br />I do appreciate that she is half-Filipino, half-Italian tho!! I love seeing all this biracial representation in YA books, because I feel like their stories are important as well.<br /><br />// <b>ADRIAN</b>: He had the potential to be a great character, but unfortunately, he joined all the other YA sacks of flour as a <b>bland character</b>. I really can’t identify any personality traits, because I’m not certain he has any??? Besides wanting to protect everyone &amp; be a selfless hero, which, let’s admit, is a pretty old &amp; boring thing we’ve seen in YA.<br /><br />Also, are we serious?? Literally NO ONE suspects that Nova is Nightmare and Adrian is the Sentinel??? (Not a spoiler btw.) “Super smart” is apparently not what any of these superheros are.<br /><br /><blockquote>🌹 <u><b>ROMANCE</b></u></blockquote><br />This book was on my “<i>need</i>” shelf? More like I <i>need</i> to find a cliff to jump off of to rid myself of this so-called “romance”.<br /><br /><b>There is literally NO chemistry between the two characters.</b> It’s so horribly forced and it’s so cringy that it makes me want to find smut to read because HONESTLY. THAT WAS HORRIBLE. ANYTHING IS BETTER THAN THAT.<br /><br />The only relationships I supported were 1) <b>ADRIAN’S GAY DADS</b>. It is not only amazing to see GAY !! ADULTS !! in YA, but amazing to see GAY !! DADS !! raising a son in a healthily-portrayed way. I also loved 2) Ruby and Oscar because it was cute, okay. And they had actual chemistry, unlike another certain forced relationship.<br /><br /><br /><br /><b>This was originally rated 2.5 stars</b>, and then I got really angry at the slowness and wanted to lower it to 1.5 stars. But !! Then the homophobic “review” happened !! So I brought it up to 2 stars because my gay dads deserve justice.<br /><br /><blockquote>// <b>buddy read</b> with my slump again, let’s hope she doesn't make me hate this 😜😜 [spoiler: it wasn’t her fault]<br /><br />(and there’s uhhhh <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/49148508-maybelline" rel="nofollow noopener">some kid</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/30283593-ilsa" rel="nofollow noopener">this kid</a> but they’re worse than the slump)</blockquote></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer3985442721665768831"><s>REVIEW TO COME TOMORROW.</s><br/><br/><b>THE REVIEW IS POSTED</b><br/><br/><b> 3.8 STARS. Totally worth to read. </b> <br/><br/><b><br/>BOLD. VALIANT. JUST. DO YOU HAVE WHAT IT TAKES TO BE A HERO?<br/></b><br/><br/>Marissa Meyer is one of my favorite authors, like I <b>need</b> to buy everything she writes. <br/>So, I bought this book because : <br/>1. Marissa Meyer is one of my favorite authors. <br/>2. The cover looked so <b>BEAUTIFUL.</b><br/>3. I needed this pretty book on my bookshelf.<br/>4. The plot was interesting.<br/><br/>Look, when my copy arrived at my house, I was beyond excited, you know. I have waited </span>
  <span id="freeText3985442721665768831" style="display:none"><s>REVIEW TO COME TOMORROW.</s><br><br><b>THE REVIEW IS POSTED</b><br><br><b> 3.8 STARS. Totally worth to read. </b> <br><br><b><br>BOLD. VALIANT. JUST. DO YOU HAVE WHAT IT TAKES TO BE A HERO?<br></b><br><br>Marissa Meyer is one of my favorite authors, like I <b>need</b> to buy everything she writes. <br>So, I bought this book because : <br>1. Marissa Meyer is one of my favorite authors. <br>2. The cover looked so <b>BEAUTIFUL.</b><br>3. I needed this pretty book on my bookshelf.<br>4. The plot was interesting.<br><br>Look, when my copy arrived at my house, I was beyond excited, you know. I have waited it for days and <b>FINALLY</b> I could touch this book and I literally hugged the book after I tore open the package and I jumped around. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1515164985ra/24836490.gif" width="300" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>but I admit that I got scared to read it because reading about superheroes was new to me but I do like watching superheroes movies but reading about them? hmm, I don't know and before I read it I had quite high expectations about this book and thank God, it lived up my expectations and it was good but I also think this book could've been better but don't worry this book was still good even though, it wasn't amazing for me. <br><br>Here are the reasons why I enjoyed reading this book : <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1515179332ra/24838052.gif" width="220" height="160" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>
  <u>The Plot and The Pacing</u>
</b><br><br>I'm not really a fan of superheroes but this book worked for me! it was good and I shouldn't have doubted this book. The plot intrigued me and it kept me that way till the end of the book, which was so great, right!? and I got even more curious, intrigued and excited when I nearly reached the ending and to be honest, I cried a little bit while reading this book but I won't talk further about why I cried because I don't want to spoil any of you and now let me tell you about the pacing.<br><br>I love reading slow-paced books <b>but</b> even though it's slow-paced, the book has to keep me interested and this book did that to me. The pacing was slow but it somehow always made me curious about ... well, everything and not every book that I have read managed to keep me interested till the end if it's slow-paced but this book, every thing was interesting and I couldn't help to feel curious and want to read more and more. <br><br><br><b>
  <u> The Characters </u>
</b><br><br>first of all, I wanted to talk about Adrian, first. Oh my God. This guy could make me smile the way I rarely smile at boys in real life! Look, I don't really need a boyfriend but I would totally be so happy if I had a boyfriend like Adrian. He is so sweet and he could make me laugh! and I rarely laugh while reading. So this means something, right?<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1515179182ra/24838020.gif" width="250" height="160" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>and about Nova, she's cool and smart and there's a particular scene that left me in awe and I even had the urge to shout her name because she was that cool and amazing. <br><br>The secondary characters in this book were also great. Especially, Oscar and Ruby. oh and Oscar was very funny and made me laugh so hard. I wish I had a friend like him! He's so precious! and I want to hug them both! and now I'm going to tell you what I didn't really like in this book.<br><br><b>
  <u>The Romance</u>
</b><br><br>It's about the romance. It's not bad and it was even good but I needed more of the romance hahaha, it wasn't enough and I totally know that the main plot here isn't the romance but ... I still needed more scenes between these two particular characters. ( if you want to find out who these characters, just read the book. IT IS GOOD :) ) <br><br><b>In conclusion, I enjoyed reading this book and had a good time reading it. I recommend you guys to read it :D </b><br><br>Thank you very much for reading and liking this review. I appreciate it very much. <b>*hugs*</b> ❤️❤️<br><br>~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~<br><b> Edit : 31/12/2017 : I tried the quiz, guys! And my super power is super strength. 💪🏻 </b> <br><br><s>
  <b> I'm currently reading it and by the way, I love the cover! It's so cool and I hope this book won't let me down. *cross fingers*<b></b></b>
</s></span>

<div id="review_2699996727" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2699996727" />
    <a title="R.K. Gold" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/40737518-r-k-gold"><img alt="R.K. Gold" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1518717825p2/40737518.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2699996727?book_show_action=true">Feb 23, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="R.K. Gold" class="user" itemprop="url" name="R.K. Gold" href="/user/show/40737518-r-k-gold">R.K. Gold</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2699996727" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5937814077026091521">This book put me in a slump. The reason I’m giving it 2 instead of 1 (and honestly it’s more of a 1.5) is cause at least it’s still a well defined story it follows basic rules of structure and someone could probably find some enjoyment from it.<br/><br/>I was not so lucky. This review will contain some spoilers because I’ll be including some of my annotations.<br/><br/>My god I’m too tired of this book to even do a deep dive. Let’s just start with how incompetent the characters are like they make every situation wo</span>
  <span id="freeText5937814077026091521" style="display:none">This book put me in a slump. The reason I’m giving it 2 instead of 1 (and honestly it’s more of a 1.5) is cause at least it’s still a well defined story it follows basic rules of structure and someone could probably find some enjoyment from it.<br /><br />I was not so lucky. This review will contain some spoilers because I’ll be including some of my annotations.<br /><br />My god I’m too tired of this book to even do a deep dive. Let’s just start with how incompetent the characters are like they make every situation worse I honestly felt like I was reading a non-comedic version of team America sometimes like there were no consequences for their actions the two main characters spent more time denying if the other person liked them or like liked them. <br /><br />Like these huge events would happen, a library would be blown up, a carnival would be the site of a huge battle, ona parade would be destroyed and nothing in their every day life changes? Like people just shrug and go on with their day is if it were just a minor annoyance. I mean they treated a terrorist attack on a public building the way I treat a cold. <br /><br />All these characters felt sooooooo flat only nova had some internal battle but it wasn’t much of a battle it was renegades are bad but this one is hot so I guess they’re alright but nah they’re bad and ya know what maybe the villains are bad too. <br /><br />The tone was all over the place. There would be a serious fight scene or dramatic event then the descriptions would be over the top comedic and characters were more interested in who could give the best one line singer than actually fighting.<br /><br />Also I usually reward books for rep but Adrian’s two gay dads had no identity beyond their sexuality. Like every time they were brought up it included a backstory of cute things they did together almost as if Meyer didn’t trust us to remember they were gay unless it was their only character identifier.<br /><br />Speaking of backstories, why did she give some I consequential a solid 2 paragraphs of exposition backstory that has no impact on the plot just to make us feel some emotion for them before they go to jail or die? Like annoyed me cause it was so manipulative.<br /><br />Ugh anyway here are my notes on this book if you want a bit of a play by play how I felt reading it. <br /><br />Ch 4: <br /><br />Why are all the descriptions comical? Aren’t they on a serious mission? There’s some tone whiplash going on <br /><br />Ugh corny banter and weapons that just happen to be there <br /><br />Ch 16<br />Rock Paper Scissors? Paper beats rock okay the dialogue is so corny <br /><br />Ch 21<br />If she wasn’t supposed to know about the Bandit why did they take her there <br /><br />Ch 23<br />This origin story scene is one info dump after another <br /><br />Ch 25<br />On what a shock the girl who walks through reflections is named narcissa, a nod to mythology to create intrigue. Okay are names personality traits now?<br /><br /><br />Ch 27<br />How many times can you write tuck and roll on one page?<br /><br />Ch 28<br />I love plot convenience. She better not trust Ingrid again<br /><br /><br />Ch 31 <br />Adrian’s dads have no identity outside of their relationship. Whenever one of them is mentioned the rest of the scene talks about how they’re married and act cute together. <br /><br />Ch 32 <br />This flirty dialogue is giving me hives<br /><br />Ch 33<br />Oscar threatened to take his tacos away? See this book tries so hard to be funny but all it does is snap my willful suspension of disbelief because Oscar isn’t coming across as funny here he’s immature and stupid in a serious scene- the tones in this book give me whiplash <br /><br />Ch 36<br /><br />Okay what’s happening that served no purpose to plot or character development just random descriptions <br /><br />Okay again these characters’ motivation seems to be witty dialogue above all else<br /><br />Ch 38<br />Unless these weapons are going to be used later I don’t need detailed descriptions and backstories of them<br /><br />Ch 39<br />I love when the protagonist is too incompetent to see their love interest likes them to create fake tension in the plot and stir some emotion for two characters I have no feelings for <br /><br />Ch 41 <br />Really she’s just now learning that the villains also caused some damage? What gave that away? The lack of consequences in this book is ridiculous. Like they blew up a library and they talk about it like a minor inconvenience. If there is a terrorist attack on your public library that’s in the news cycle constantly the city reshapes people would revisit security laws—everyone just shrugged <br /><br />They are such kids and it’s not cute since they’re also police officers like I get it teens care about romance more than anything else but maybe this society would’ve figured that out by now and not put teens in charge no matter how powerful they are<br /><br />Ch 42<br />I rolled my eyes so hard at Adrian’s dialogue that I think I concusses myself<br /><br />Ch 44 <br />He really just discovered the villain named the detonator has the ability to detonate things? How stupid is this guy? Also why does Nova keep trusting Ingrid she’s done nothing but betray her.<br /><br />Wow she really can’t figure out they’re planning on using the bandit to steal powers? They literally said it involves max and that soon they won’t have to deal with people’s powers anymore. How blatant can they get?</span>
  <a data-text-id="5937814077026091521" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/34389079-renegades">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=kindle">kindle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=2018">2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=library">library</a>
